href="http://www.manchester.ac.uk/">manchester.ac.uk</a></td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/File:UniOfManchesterLogo.svg" class="image"><img alt="UniOfManchesterLogo.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/72/UniOfManchesterLogo.svg/250px-UniOfManchesterLogo.svg.png" width="250" height="105" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/72/UniOfManchesterLogo.svg/375px-UniOfManchesterLogo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/72/UniOfManchesterLogo.svg/500px-UniOfManchesterLogo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="216" /></a></td>/n</tr>/n</table>/n<p><b>The University of Manchester</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a> <a href="/wiki/Research_universities" class="mw-redirect" title="Research universities">research university</a> in <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>, England, formed in 2004 by the merger of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Manchester_Institute_of_Science_and_Technology" title="University of Manchester Institute of Science and Technology">University of Manchester Institute of Science and Technology</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Victoria_University_of_Manchester" title="Victoria University of Manchester">Victoria University of Manchester</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> The University of Manchester is a <a href="/wiki/Red_brick_university" title="Red brick university">red brick university</a>, a product of the civic university movement of the late-19th century.</p>/n<p>The main campus is south of <a href="/wiki/Manchester_city_centre" title="Manchester city centre">Manchester city centre</a> on <a href="/wiki/Wilmslow_Road" title="Wilmslow Road">Oxford Road</a>. In 2015/16, the university had 39,700 students and 10,400 staff, making it the <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_the_United_Kingdom_by_enrollment" class="mw-redirect" title="List of universities in the United Kingdom by enrollment">second largest</a> university in the UK (out of 166 including the <a href="/wiki/Open_University" title="Open University">Open University</a>), and the largest single-site university. The university had a consolidated income of £987.2 million in 2015–16, of which £273.5 million was from research grants and contracts.<sup id="cite_ref-finstat_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finstat-1">[1]</a></sup> It has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_UK_universities_by_endowment" title="List of UK universities by endowment">third largest endowment</a> of any university in England, after the universities of <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Cambridge University">Cambridge</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oxford_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Oxford University">Oxford</a>. It is a member of the worldwide <a href="/wiki/Universities_Research_Association" title="Universities Research Association">Universities Research Association</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Russell_Group" title="Russell Group">Russell Group</a> of British research universities and the <a href="/wiki/N8_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="N8 Group">N8 Group</a>.</p>/n<p>In 2016-17, the University of Manchester was ranked 55th in the world and 8th in the UK by <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a>, 34th in the world and 7th in the UK by <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a>, 35th in the world and 5th in the UK by <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a><sup id="cite_ref-Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities_2016_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities_2016-8">[8]</a></sup> and 59th in the world by <a href="/wiki/U.S._News_and_World_Report" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. News and World Report">U.S. News and World Report</a>. In the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Research_Assessment_Exercise" title="Research Assessment Exercise">Research Assessment Exercise</a>, Manchester was named as the 17th best research institution in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>/n<p>The university owns and operates major cultural assets such as the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Museum" title="Manchester Museum">Manchester Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Whitworth_Art_Gallery" title="Whitworth Art Gallery">Whitworth Art Gallery</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Rylands_Library" title="John Rylands Library">John Rylands Library</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jodrell_Bank_Observatory" title="Jodrell Bank Observatory">Jodrell Bank Observatory</a> and its Grade I listed <a href="/wiki/Lovell_Telescope" title="Lovell Telescope">Lovell Telescope</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>/n<p>The University of Manchester has <a href="/wiki/University_of_Manchester#Nobel_prize_winners" title="University of Manchester">25 Nobel laureates</a> among its past and present students and staff, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_by_university_affiliation" title="List of Nobel laureates by university affiliation">fourth-highest number of any single university</a> in the United Kingdom. Four Nobel laureates are currently among its staff – more than any other British university.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>/n<div class="toclimit-3">/n<div id="toc" class="toc">/n<div class="toctitle">/n<h2>Contents</h2>/n</div>/n<ul>/n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Academic profile</span></a>/n<ul>/n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Research"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span Manchester Library</span></a></li>/n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a href="#Collections"><span class="tocnumber">4.3</span> <span class="toctext">Collections</span></a>/n<ul>/n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-20"><a href="#Manchester_Museum"><span class="tocnumber">4.3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Manchester Museum</span></a></li>/n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-21"><a href="#Whitworth_Art_Gallery"><span class="tocnumber">4.3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Whitworth Art Gallery</span></a></li>/n</ul>/n</li>/n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a class="toctext">Manchester University Press</span></a></li>/n</ul>/n</li>/n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#Student_life"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Student life</span></a>/n<ul>/n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26"><a href="#Students.27_Union"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Students' Union</span></a></li>/n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#Sport"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">Sport</span></a></li>/n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28"><a href="#University_Challenge_quiz_programme"><span class="tocnumber">5.3</span> <span class="toctext"><i>University Challenge</i> quiz programme</span></a></li>/n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"><a href="#Overseas_students"><span class="tocnumber">5.4</span> <span class="toctext">Overseas students</span></a></li>/n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#Student_housing"><span class="tocnumber">5.5</span> <span class="toctext">Student housing</span></a>/n<ul>/n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-31"><a href="#City_Campus"><span class="tocnumber">5.5.1</span> <span class="toctext">City Campus</span></a>/n<ul>/n<li class="toclevel-4 tocsection-32"><a href="#Whitworth_Park_Halls_of_Residence"><span class="tocnumber">5.5.1.1</span> <span class="toctext">Whitworth Park Halls of Residence</span></a></li>/n<li class="toclevel-4 tocsection-33"><a href="#Sackville_Street"><span class="tocnumber">5.5.1.2</span> <span class="toctext">Sackville Street</span></a></li>/n</ul>/n</li>/n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-34"><a href="#Victoria_Park_Campus"><span class="tocnumber">5.5.2</span> <span class="toctext">Victoria Park Campus</span></a></li>/n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-35"><a href="#Fallowfield_Campus"><span class="tocnumber">5.5.3</span> <span class="toctext">Fallowfield Campus</span></a></li>/n</ul>/n</li>/n</ul>/n</li>/n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-36"><a href="#Notable_people"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Notable people</span></a>/n<ul>/n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-37"><a href="#Nobel_prize_winners"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Nobel prize winners</span></a></li>/n</ul>/n</li>/n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-38"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>/n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-39"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>/n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-40"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>/n</ul>/n</div>/n</div>/n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/UMIST" class="mw-redirect" title="UMIST">UMIST</a> and <a href="/wiki/Victoria_University_of_Manchester" title="Victoria University of Manchester">Victoria University of Manchester</a></div>/n<div class="thumb tright">/n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_Quadrangle,_Manchester_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Old_Quadrangle%2C_Manchester_1.jpg/220px-Old_Quadrangle%2C_Manchester_1.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Old_Quadrangle%2C_Manchester_1.jpg/330px-Old_Quadrangle%2C_Manchester_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Old_Quadrangle%2C_Manchester_1.jpg/440px-Old_Quadrangle%2C_Manchester_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592" /></a>/n<div class="thumbcaption">/n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_Quadrangle,_Manchester_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>/nThe Old Quadrangle at the University of Manchester's main campus on Oxford Road.</div>/n</div>/n</div>/n<p>The University of Manchester traces its roots to the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Mechanics%27_Institute,_Manchester" title="Mechanics' Institute, Manchester">Mechanics' Institute</a> (later <a href="/wiki/UMIST" class="mw-redirect" title="UMIST">UMIST</a>) in 1824, and its heritage is linked to Manchester's pride in being the world's first industrial city.<sup id="cite_ref-Our_History_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Our_History-12">[12]</a></sup> The English <a href="/wiki/Chemist" title="Chemist">chemist</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Dalton" title="John Dalton">John Dalton</a>, together with Manchester businessmen and industrialists, established the Mechanics' Institute to ensure that workers could learn the basic principles of science.</p>/n<p><a href="/wiki/John_Owens_(merchant)" title="John Owens (merchant)">John Owens</a>, a textile merchant, left a bequest of £96,942 in 1846 (around £5.6 million in 2005 prices)<sup id="cite_ref-National_Archives_Currency_Converter_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-National_Archives_Currency_Converter-13">[13]</a></sup> to found a college to educate men on non-sectarian lines. His <a href="/wiki/Trustee" title="Trustee">trustees</a> established <a href="/wiki/Owens_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Owens College">Owens College</a> in 1851 in a house on the corner of <a href="/wiki/Quay_Street" title="Quay Street">Quay Street</a> and Byrom Street which had been the home of the philanthropist <a href="/wiki/Richard_Cobden" title="Richard Cobden">Richard Cobden</a>, and subsequently housed <a href="/wiki/County_Court,_Manchester" title="County Court, Manchester">Manchester County Court</a>. The locomotive designer, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Beyer" title="Charles Beyer">Charles Beyer</a> became a governor of the college and was the largest single donor to the college extension fund, which raised the money to move to a new site and construct the main building now known as the John Owens building. He also campaigned and helped fund the engineering chair, the first applied science department in the north of England. He left the college the equivalent of £10 million in his will in 1876, at a time when it was in great financial difficulty. Beyer funded the total cost of construction of <a href="/wiki/The_Beyer_building_(University_of_Manchester)" title="The Beyer building (University of Manchester)">the Beyer building</a> to house the biology and geology departments. His will also funded Engineering chairs and the <a href="/wiki/Beyer_Professor_of_Applied_Mathematics" title="Beyer Professor of Applied Mathematics">Beyer Professor of Applied mathematics</a>.</p>/n<p>The university has a rich German heritage. The Owens College Extension Movement based their plans after a tour of mainly German universities and polytechnics.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Manchester mill owner, Thomas Ashton, chairman of the extension movement had studied at <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg_University" title="Heidelberg University">Heidelberg University</a>. <a href="/wiki/Henry_Enfield_Roscoe" class="mw-redirect" title="Henry Enfield Roscoe">Sir Henry Roscoe</a> also studied at Heidelberg under Robert Bunsen and they collaborated for many years on research projects. Roscoe promoted the German style of research led teaching that became the role model for the redbrick universities. Charles Beyer studied at Dresden Academy Polytechnic. There were many Germans on the staff, including <a href="/wiki/Carl_Schorlemmer" title="Carl Schorlemmer">Carl Schorlemmer</a>, Britain's first chair in organic chemistry, and <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Schuster" title="Arthur Schuster">Arthur Schuster</a>, professor of Physics.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> There was even a German chapel on the campus.</p>/n<p>In 1873 the college moved to new premises on Oxford Road, <a href="/wiki/Chorlton-on-Medlock" title="Chorlton-on-Medlock">Chorlton-on-Medlock</a> and from 1880 it was a constituent college of the <a href="/wiki/Victoria_University_(United_Kingdom)" title="Victoria University (United Kingdom)">federal Victoria University</a>. The university was established and granted a <a href="/wiki/Royal_Charter" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Charter">Royal Charter</a> in 1880 becoming England's first civic university; it was renamed the <a href="/wiki/Victoria_University_of_Manchester" title="Victoria University of Manchester">Victoria University of Manchester</a> in 1903 and absorbed Owens College the following year.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> By 1905, the institutions were large and active forces. The Municipal College of Technology, forerunner of UMIST, was the Victoria University of Manchester's Faculty of Technology while continuing in parallel as a technical college offering advanced courses of study. Although UMIST achieved independent university status in 1955, the universities continued to work together.<sup id="cite_ref-History_and_Origins_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_and_Origins-18">[18]</a></sup> However, in the late-20th century, formal connections between the university and UMIST diminished and in 1994 most of the remaining institutional ties were severed as new legislation allowed UMIST to become an autonomous university with powers to award its own degrees. A decade later the development was reversed.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> The Victoria University of Manchester and the University of Manchester Institute of Science and Technology agreed to merge into a single institution in March 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>/n<p>Before the merger, Victoria University of Manchester and UMIST counted 23 Nobel Prize winners amongst their former staff and students. Manchester has traditionally been strong in the sciences; it is where the nuclear nature of the atom was discovered by <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Rutherford" title="Ernest Rutherford">Ernest Rutherford</a>, and the world's <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Small-Scale_Experimental_Machine" title="Manchester Small-Scale Experimental Machine">first stored-program computer</a> was built at the university. Notable scientists associated with the university include <a href="/wiki/Physicist" title="Physicist">physicists</a> Ernest Rutherford, <a href="/wiki/Osborne_Reynolds" title="Osborne Reynolds">Osborne Reynolds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Niels_Bohr" title="Niels Bohr">Niels Bohr</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Chadwick" title="James Chadwick">James Chadwick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Schuster" title="Arthur Schuster">Arthur Schuster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hans_Geiger" title="Hans Geiger">Hans Geiger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Marsden" title="Ernest Marsden">Ernest Marsden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Balfour_Stewart" title="Balfour Stewart">Balfour Stewart</a>. Contributions in other fields such as mathematics were made by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Erd%C5%91s" title="Paul Erdős">Paul Erdős</a>, <a href="/wiki/Horace_Lamb" title="Horace Lamb">Horace Lamb</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alan_Turing" title="Alan Turing">Alan Turing</a> and in philosophy by <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Alexander" title="Samuel Alexander">Samuel Alexander</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_Wittgenstein" title="Ludwig Wittgenstein">Ludwig Wittgenstein</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alasdair_MacIntyre" title="Alasdair MacIntyre">Alasdair MacIntyre</a>. The author <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Burgess" title="Anthony Burgess">Anthony Burgess</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pritzker_Prize" class="mw-redirect" title="Pritzker Prize">Pritzker Prize</a> and <a href="/wiki/RIBA_Stirling_Prize" class="mw-redirect" title="RIBA Stirling Prize">RIBA Stirling Prize</a>-winning architect <a href="/wiki/Norman_Foster,_Baron_Foster_of_Thames_Bank" title="Norman Foster, Baron Foster of Thames Bank">Norman Foster</a> and composer <a href="/wiki/Peter_Maxwell_Davies" title="Peter Maxwell Davies">Peter Maxwell Davies</a> all attended, or worked at, Manchester.</p>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2004_to_present">2004 to present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 2004 to present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<div class="thumb tright">/n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UMIST_Sackville_Street_Building.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/UMIST_Sackville_Street_Building.jpg/220px-UMIST_Sackville_Street_Building.jpg" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/UMIST_Sackville_Street_Building.jpg/330px-UMIST_Sackville_Street_Building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/UMIST_Sackville_Street_Building.jpg/440px-UMIST_Sackville_Street_Building.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="482" /></a>/n<div class="thumbcaption">/n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UMIST_Sackville_Street_Building.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>/nThe <a href="/wiki/Sackville_Street_Building" title="Sackville Street Building">Sackville Street Building</a>, formerly the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Manchester_Institute_of_Science_and_Technology" title="University of Manchester Institute of Science and Technology">UMIST</a> Main Building</div>/n</div>/n</div>/n<p>The current University of Manchester was officially launched on 1 October 2004 when <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Elizabeth II of the United Kingdom">Queen Elizabeth</a> handed over its <a href="/wiki/Royal_Charter" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Charter">Royal Charter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The university was named the <a href="/wiki/Sunday_Times_University_of_the_Year" title="Sunday Times University of the Year"><i>Sunday Times</i> University of the Year</a> in 2006 after winning the inaugural <i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_Supplement" class="mw-redirect" title="Times Higher Education Supplement">Times Higher Education Supplement</a></i> University of the Year prize in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>/n<p>The founding president and <a href="/wiki/Vice-chancellor_(education)" class="mw-redirect" title="Vice-chancellor (education)">vice-chancellor</a> of the new university was <a href="/wiki/Alan_Gilbert_(Australian_academic)" title="Alan Gilbert (Australian academic)">Alan Gilbert</a>, former Vice-Chancellor of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Melbourne" title="University of Melbourne">University of Melbourne</a>, who retired at the end of the 2009–2010 academic year.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> His successor was Dame <a href="/wiki/Nancy_Rothwell" title="Nancy Rothwell">Nancy Rothwell</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-rothswho_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rothswho-3">[3]</a></sup> who had held a chair in physiology at the university since 1994. One of the university's aims stated in the <i>Manchester 2015 Agenda</i> is to be one of the top 25 universities in the world, following on from Alan Gilbert's aim to "establish it by 2015 among the 25 strongest research universities in the world on commonly accepted criteria of research excellence and performance".<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> In 2011, four Nobel laureates were on its staff: <a href="/wiki/Andre_Geim" title="Andre Geim">Andre Geim</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-geims_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geims-26">[26]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Konstantin_Novoselov" title="Konstantin Novoselov">Konstantin Novoselov</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-novswho_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-novswho-27">[27]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Sulston" title="John Sulston">Sir John Sulston</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joseph_E._Stiglitz" class="mw-redirect" title="Joseph E. Stiglitz">Joseph E. Stiglitz</a>.</p>/n<p>The <a href="/wiki/EPSRC" class="mw-redirect" title="EPSRC">EPSRC</a> announced in February 2012 the formation of the <a href="/wiki/National_Graphene_Institute" title="National Graphene Institute">National Graphene Institute</a>. The University of Manchester is the "single supplier invited to submit a proposal for funding the new £45m institute, £38m of which will be provided by the government" – (EPSRC &amp; <a href="/wiki/Technology_Strategy_Board" class="mw-redirect" title="Technology Strategy Board">Technology Strategy Board</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> In 2013, an additional £23 million of funding from European Regional Development Fund was awarded to the institute taking investment to £61 million.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>/n<p>In August 2012, it was announced that the university's Faculty of Engineering and Physical Sciences had been chosen to be the "hub" location for a new <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.icam-online.org/">BP International Centre for Advanced Materials</a>, as part of a $100 million initiative to create industry-changing materials.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> The centre will be aimed at advancing fundamental understanding and use of materials across a variety of oil and gas industrial applications and will be modelled on a hub and spoke structure, with the hub located at Manchester, and the spokes based at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">University of Cambridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Imperial_College_London" title="Imperial College London">Imperial College London</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana-Champaign" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Illinois at Urbana-Champaign">University of Illinois at Urbana-Champaign</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BP_Pledges_.24100_Million_to_UK-Led_Universities_to_Create_Industry-Changing_Materials_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BP_Pledges_.24100_Million_to_UK-Led_Universities_to_Create_Industry-Changing_Materials-32">[32]</a></sup></p>/n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>/n<p>The university's main site contains most of its facilities and is often referred to as <i>campus</i>, however Manchester is not a <a href="/wiki/Campus_university" title="Campus university">campus university</a> as the concept is commonly understood. It is centrally located in the city and its buildings are integrated into the fabric of Manchester, with non-university buildings and major roads between.</p>/n<p>The campus occupies an area shaped roughly like a boot: the foot of which is aligned roughly south-west to north-east and is joined to the broader southern part of the boot by an area of overlap between former UMIST and former VUM buildings;<sup id="cite_ref-googleCampusMap_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-googleCampusMap-33">[33]</a></sup> it comprises two parts:</p>/n<ul>/n<li><i>North campus</i> or <i>Sackville Street Campus</i>, centred on <a href="/wiki/Sackville_Street_(Manchester)" title="Sackville Street (Manchester)">Sackville Street</a></li>/n<li><i>South campus</i> or <i>Oxford Road Campus</i>, centred on <a href="/wiki/Oxford_Road,_Manchester" class="mw-redirect" title="Oxford Road, Manchester">Oxford Road</a>.</li>/n</ul>/n<p>The names are not officially recognised by the university, but are commonly used, including in parts of its website and roughly correspond to the campuses of the old UMIST and Victoria University respectively.</p>/n<p><a href="/wiki/Fallowfield_Campus" title="Fallowfield Campus">Fallowfield Campus</a> is the main residential campus in <a href="/wiki/Fallowfield" title="Fallowfield">Fallowfield</a>, approximately 2 miles (3&#160;km) south of the main site.</p>/n<p>There are other university buildings across the city and the wider region, such as <a href="/wiki/Jodrell_Bank_Observatory" title="Jodrell Bank Observatory">Jodrell Bank Observatory</a> in Cheshire and One Central Park in Moston, a collaboration between the university and other partners which offers office space for start-up firms and venues for conferences and workshops,<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_projects">Major projects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Major projects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<div class="thumb tright">/n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MIBatrium.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/MIBatrium.jpg/220px-MIBatrium.jpg" width="220" height="296" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/MIBatrium.jpg/330px-MIBatrium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/MIBatrium.jpg/440px-MIBatrium.jpg 2x" data-file-width="479" data-file-height="645" /></a>/n<div class="thumbcaption">/n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MIBatrium.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>/nThe atrium inside the £38m <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Institute_of_Biotechnology" title="Manchester Institute of Biotechnology">Manchester Institute of Biotechnology</a></div>/n</div>/n</div>/n<p>Following the merger, the university embarked on a £600 million programme of capital investment, to deliver eight new buildings and 15 major refurbishment projects by 2010, partly financed by a sale of unused assets.<sup id="cite_ref-AssetSale_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AssetSale-35">[35]</a></sup> These include:</p>/n<ul>/n<li>£60 m Flagship <i>University Place</i> building (new)</li>/n<li>£56 m <a href="/wiki/Alan_Turing_Building" title="Alan Turing Building">Alan Turing Building</a> houses <a href="/wiki/School_of_Mathematics,_University_of_Manchester" title="School of Mathematics, University of Manchester">Mathematics</a>, replaced <a href="/wiki/Mathematics_Tower,_Manchester" title="Mathematics Tower, Manchester">Mathematics Tower</a>. Home to the Photon Sciences Institute and the <a href="/wiki/Jodrell_Bank_Centre_for_Astrophysics" title="Jodrell Bank Centre for Astrophysics">Jodrell Bank Centre for Astrophysics</a> (new)</li>/n<li>£50 m Life Sciences Research Building (A. V. Hill Building) (new)</li>/n<li>£38 m <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Institute_of_Biotechnology" title="Manchester Institute of Biotechnology">Manchester Institute of Biotechnology</a> (MIB) (new)</li>/n<li>£33 m Life Sciences and Medical and Human Sciences Building (Michael Smith Building) (new)</li>/n<li>£31 m Humanities Building – now officially called the "<a href="/wiki/Arthur_Lewis_Building" title="Arthur Lewis Building">Arthur Lewis Building</a>" (new)</li>/n<li>£20 m <a href="/wiki/Wolfson_Molecular_Imaging_Centre" title="Wolfson Molecular Imaging Centre">Wolfson Molecular Imaging Centre</a> (WMIC) (new)</li>/n<li>£18 m Re-location of School of Pharmacy</li>/n<li>£17 m <a href="/wiki/John_Rylands_Library" title="John Rylands Library">John Rylands Library</a>, Deansgate (extension &amp; refurbishment of existing building)</li>/n<li>£13 m Chemistry Building</li>/n<li>£10 m Functional Biology Building</li>/n</ul>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Old_Quadrangle">Old Quadrangle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Old Quadrangle">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<p>The buildings around the Old Quadrangle date from the time of Owens College, and were designed in a <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic</a> style by <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Waterhouse" title="Alfred Waterhouse">Alfred Waterhouse</a> and his son <a href="/wiki/Paul_Waterhouse" title="Paul Waterhouse">Paul Waterhouse</a>. The first to be built was the John Owens Building (1873), formerly the Main Building; the others were added over the next thirty years. Today, <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Museum" title="Manchester Museum">the museum</a> continues to occupy part of one side, including the tower. The grand setting of the <a href="/wiki/Whitworth_Hall" title="Whitworth Hall">Whitworth Hall</a> is used for the conferment of degrees, and part of the old <a href="/wiki/R._C._Christie" class="mw-redirect" title="R. C. Christie">Christie Library</a> (1898) now houses Christie's Bistro. The remainder of the buildings house administrative departments. The less easily accessed Rear Quadrangle, dating mostly from 1873, is older in its completed form than the Old Quadrangle.</p>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contact">Contact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Contact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<div class="thumb tleft">/n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Contact_Theatre_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Contact_Theatre_2009.jpg/220px-Contact_Theatre_2009.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Contact_Theatre_2009.jpg/330px-Contact_Theatre_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Contact_Theatre_2009.jpg/440px-Contact_Theatre_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2580" data-file-height="1720" /></a>/n<div class="thumbcaption">/n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Contact_Theatre_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>/nThe <a href="/wiki/Contact_Theatre" title="Contact Theatre">Contact Theatre</a></div>/n</div>/n</div>/n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Contact_Theatre" title="Contact Theatre">Contact Theatre</a></div>/n<p>Contact stages modern live performance for all ages, and participatory workshops primarily for young people aged 13 to 30. The building on Devas Street was completed in 1999 incorporating parts of its 1960s predecessor.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> It has a unique energy-efficient ventilation system, using its high towers to naturally ventilate the building without the use of air conditioning. The colourful and curvaceous interior houses three performance spaces, a lounge bar and <i>Hot Air</i>, a reactive public artwork in the foyer.</p>/n<div class="thumb tright">/n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UOMCampusmap.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/UOMCampusmap.jpg/220px-UOMCampusmap.jpg" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/UOMCampusmap.jpg/330px-UOMCampusmap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/UOMCampusmap.jpg/440px-UOMCampusmap.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1224" data-file-height="761" /></a>/n<div class="thumbcaption">/n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UOMCampusmap.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>/nA map of the university campus, with all buildings labelled.</div>/n</div>/n</div>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chancellors_Hotel_and_Conference_Centre">Chancellors Hotel and Conference Centre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Chancellors Hotel and Conference Centre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Conference_Centre" title="Manchester Conference Centre">Manchester Conference Centre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chancellors_Hotel_%26_Conference_Centre" title="Chancellors Hotel &amp; Conference Centre">Chancellors Hotel &amp; Conference Centre</a></div>/n<div class="thumb tright">/n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chcc_blue_sky.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Chcc_blue_sky.jpg/220px-Chcc_blue_sky.jpg" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Chcc_blue_sky.jpg/330px-Chcc_blue_sky.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Chcc_blue_sky.jpg/440px-Chcc_blue_sky.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="518" /></a>/n<div class="thumbcaption">/n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chcc_blue_sky.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>/nChancellors Hotel &amp; Conference Centre</div>/n</div>/n</div>/n<p>The Chancellors Hotel &amp; Conference Centre was built around The Firs, a house built in 1850 for <a href="/wiki/Sir_Joseph_Whitworth" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Joseph Whitworth">Sir Joseph Whitworth</a> by <a href="/wiki/Edward_Walters" title="Edward Walters">Edward Walters</a>, who also designed Manchester's <a href="/wiki/Free_Trade_Hall" title="Free Trade Hall">Free Trade Hall</a>. Whitworth used the house as a social, political and business base, entertaining radicals such as <a href="/wiki/John_Bright" title="John Bright">John Bright</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Cobden" title="Richard Cobden">Richard Cobden</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Edward_Forster" title="William Edward Forster">William Forster</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Henry_Huxley" title="Thomas Henry Huxley">T.H. Huxley</a> at the time of the <a href="/wiki/Reform_Bill" class="mw-redirect" title="Reform Bill">Reform Bill</a> of 1867. Whitworth, credited with raising the art of machine-tool building to a previously unknown level, supported the <a href="/wiki/Mechanics_Institute" class="mw-redirect" title="Mechanics Institute">Mechanics Institute</a> – the birthplace of <a href="/wiki/UMIST" class="mw-redirect" title="UMIST">UMIST</a> – and was a founder the Manchester School of Design. Whilst living there, Whitworth used land at the rear (now the site of the University's botanical glasshouses) for testing his "<a href="/wiki/Whitworth_rifle" title="Whitworth rifle">Whitworth rifle</a>". In 1882, The Firs was leased to <a href="/wiki/C.P._Scott" class="mw-redirect" title="C.P. Scott">C.P. Scott</a>, editor of the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Guardian" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Guardian">Manchester Guardian</a> and after Scott's death became the property of <a href="/wiki/Owens_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Owens College">Owens College</a>. It was the Vice-Chancellor's residence until 1991.</p>/n<p>The house now forms the western wing of the Chancellors Hotel &amp; Conference Centre. The eastern wing houses the circular Flowers Theatre, six conference rooms and most of the hotel's bedrooms.</p>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_notable_buildings">Other notable buildings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Other notable buildings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<p>Other notable buildings in the Oxford Road Campus include the <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Joseph_Studio" title="Stephen Joseph Studio">Stephen Joseph Studio</a>, a former German Protestant church and the <b>Samuel Alexander Building</b>, a <a href="/wiki/Grade_II_listed_building" class="mw-redirect" title="Grade II listed building">grade II listed building</a><sup id="cite_ref-English_Heritage_-_List_Entry_Summary_-_Samuel_Alexander_Building_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-English_Heritage_-_List_Entry_Summary_-_Samuel_Alexander_Building-37">[37]</a></sup> erected in 1919 and home of the School of Arts, Languages and Cultures.</p>/n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organisation_and_administration">Organisation and administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Organisation and administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculties_and_schools">Faculties and schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Faculties and schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<p>The University of Manchester was divided into four faculties, but from 1 August 2016 it was restructured into three faculties, each sub-divided into schools.</p>/n<p>On 25 June 2015 Manchester University announced the results of a review of the position of life sciences as a separate faculty. As a result of this review the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Manchester_Faculty_of_Life_Sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Manchester Faculty of Life Sciences">Faculty of Life Sciences</a> was to be dismantled, most of its personnel to be incorporated into a single medical/biological faculty, with a substantial minority being incorporated into a science and engineering faculty.</p>/n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculty_of_Biology_Medicine_and_Health">Faculty of Biology Medicine and Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Faculty of Biology Medicine and Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>/n<div class="thumb tright">/n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_Medical_School.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1f/Old_Medical_School.jpg/220px-Old_Medical_School.jpg" width="220" height="190" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1f/Old_Medical_School.jpg/330px-Old_Medical_School.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/1/1f/Old_Medical_School.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="346" /></a>/n<div class="thumbcaption">/n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_Medical_School.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>/nOld Medical School on Coupland Street (photographed in 1908), which now houses the School of Dentistry</div>/n</div>/n</div>/n<p>The faculty is divided into the School of Biological Sciences, the School of Medical Sciences and the School of Health Sciences.</p>/n<p>Biological Sciences have been taught at Manchester as far back as the foundation of Owens College in 1851. At UMIST, biological teaching and research began in 1959, with the creation of a Biochemistry department.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The present school, though unitary for teaching, is divided into a number of sections for research purposes.</p>/n<p>The medical college was established in 1874 and is one of the largest in the country,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> with more than 400 medical students trained in each clinical year and more than 350 students in the pre-clinical/phase 1 years.</p>/n<p>The university is a founding partner of the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Academic_Health_Science_Centre" title="Manchester Academic Health Science Centre">Manchester Academic Health Science Centre</a>, established to focus high-end healthcare research in Greater Manchester.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>/n<p>In 1883, a department of pharmacy was established at the university and, in 1904, Manchester became the first British university to offer an honours degree in the subject. The School of Pharmacy<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> benefits from links with Manchester Royal Infirmary and Wythenshawe and Hope hospitals providing its undergraduate students with hospital experience.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> The Pharmacy School's <a href="/wiki/Centre_for_Pharmacy_Postgraduate_Education" title="Centre for Pharmacy Postgraduate Education">Centre for Pharmacy Postgraduate Education</a> (CPPE) is considered a centre of excellence.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>/n<p>Manchester Dental School was rated the country's best dental school by <i>Times Higher Education</i> in 2010 and 2011<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> and it is one of the best funded because of its emphasis on research and enquiry-based learning approach. The university has obtained multimillion-pound backing to maintain its high standard of <a href="/wiki/Dental_education" class="mw-redirect" title="Dental education">dental education</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> The University Dental Hospital of Manchester is part of Central Manchester University Hospitals NHS Foundation Trust. It was established in 1884 in association with the School of Medicine at Owens College. In 1905 the university established a degree and a diploma in <a href="/wiki/Dental_surgery" title="Dental surgery">dental surgery</a> (first awarded in 1909 and 1908 respectively).<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>/n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculty_of_Science_and_Engineering">Faculty of Science and Engineering</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Faculty of Science and Engineering">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>/n<div class="thumb tright">/n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Field_towards_Jodrell_Bank_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1499278.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Field_towards_Jodrell_Bank_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1499278.jpg/220px-Field_towards_Jodrell_Bank_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1499278.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Field_towards_Jodrell_Bank_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1499278.jpg/330px-Field_towards_Jodrell_Bank_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1499278.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Field_towards_Jodrell_Bank_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1499278.jpg/440px-Field_towards_Jodrell_Bank_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1499278.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>/n<div class="thumbcaption">/n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Field_towards_Jodrell_Bank_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1499278.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>/nThe Grade I listed <a href="/wiki/Lovell_Telescope" title="Lovell Telescope">Lovell Telescope</a> at <a href="/wiki/Jodrell_Bank_Observatory" title="Jodrell Bank Observatory">Jodrell Bank Observatory</a>.</div>/n</div>/n</div>/n<p>The <b>Faculty of Science and Engineering</b> comprises the schools of <i><a href="/wiki/School_of_Chemical_Engineering_and_Analytical_Sciences,_University_of_Manchester" title="School of Chemical Engineering and Analytical Sciences, University of Manchester">Chemical Engineering and Analytical Science</a></i>;<i><a href="/wiki/School_of_Chemistry,_University_of_Manchester" title="School of Chemistry, University of Manchester">Chemistry</a></i>; <i><a href="/wiki/School_of_Computer_Science,_University_of_Manchester" title="School of Computer Science, University of Manchester">Computer Science</a></i>; <i>Earth and Environmental Science</i>; <i><a href="/wiki/School_of_Physics_and_Astronomy,_University_of_Manchester" title="School of Physics and Astronomy, University of Manchester">Physics and Astronomy</a></i>; <i><a href="/wiki/School_of_Electrical_and_Electronic_Engineering,_University_of_Manchester" title="School of Electrical and Electronic Engineering, University of Manchester">Electrical and Electronic Engineering</a></i>; <i><a href="/wiki/School_of_Materials,_University_of_Manchester" title="School of Materials, University of Manchester">Materials</a></i>; <i><a href="/wiki/School_of_Mathematics,_University_of_Manchester" title="School of Mathematics, University of Manchester">Mathematics</a></i>; and <i><a href="/wiki/School_of_Mechanical,_Aerospace_and_Civil_Engineering" class="mw-redirect" title="School of Mechanical, Aerospace and Civil Engineering">Mechanical, Aerospace and Civil Engineering</a></i>.</p>/n<p>The Jodrell Bank Centre for Astrophysics comprises the university's astronomical academic staff in Manchester and <a href="/wiki/Jodrell_Bank_Observatory" title="Jodrell Bank Observatory">Jodrell Bank Observatory</a> on rural land near <a href="/wiki/Goostrey" title="Goostrey">Goostrey</a>, about ten miles (16&#160;km) west of <a href="/wiki/Macclesfield" title="Macclesfield">Macclesfield</a> away from the lights of Greater Manchester. The observatory's <a href="/wiki/Lovell_Telescope" title="Lovell Telescope">Lovell Telescope</a>, named after Sir <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Lovell" title="Bernard Lovell">Bernard Lovell</a>, a professor at the <a href="/wiki/Victoria_University_of_Manchester" title="Victoria University of Manchester">Victoria University of Manchester</a> who first proposed the telescope. Constructed in the 1950s, it is the third largest fully movable radio telescope in the world. It has played an important role in the research of <a href="/wiki/Quasar" title="Quasar">quasars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pulsar" title="Pulsar">pulsars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gravitational_lens" title="Gravitational lens">gravitational lenses</a>, and in confirming <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">Einstein's</a> theory of <a href="/wiki/General_Relativity" class="mw-redirect" title="General Relativity">General Relativity</a>. A £1.2 billion <a href="/wiki/Square_Kilometre_Array" title="Square Kilometre Array">Square Kilometre Array</a> with 50 times more sensitivity and the ability to search space 10,000 times faster than any other telescope in existence will become operational in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>/n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculty_of_Humanities">Faculty of Humanities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Faculty of Humanities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>/n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Faculty_of_Humanities_(University_of_Manchester)" class="mw-redirect" title="Faculty of Humanities (University of Manchester)">Faculty of Humanities</a> includes the School of Arts, Languages and Cultures (incorporating Archaeology; Art History &amp; Visual Studies; Classics and Ancient History; Drama; English and American Studies; History; Linguistics; Modern Languages; Museology; Music; Religions and Theology and the University Language Centre) and the Schools of Combined Studies; Education; Environment and Development; <a href="/wiki/Manchester_School_of_Architecture" title="Manchester School of Architecture">Architecture</a>; Law; <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Lewis_Building" title="Arthur Lewis Building">Social Sciences</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Business_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Business School">Manchester Business School</a>. The Faculty of Humanities also jointly administers the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_School_of_Architecture" title="Manchester School of Architecture">Manchester School of Architecture</a> (MSA) in conjunction with <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Metropolitan_University" title="Manchester Metropolitan University">Manchester Metropolitan University</a> and MSA students are classified as students of both universities.</p>/n<p>Additionally, the faculty comprises a number of research institutes: the Centre for New Writing, the Institute for Social Change, the Brooks World Poverty Institute, Humanitarian and Conflict Response Institute, the Manchester Institute for Innovation Research, the Research Institute for Cosmopolitan Cultures, the Centre for Chinese Studies, the Institute for Development Policy and Management, the Centre for Equity in Education and the Sustainable Consumption Institute.</p>/n<div class="thumb tright">/n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Whitworth_Hall_Manchester.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Whitworth_Hall_Manchester.jpg/220px-Whitworth_Hall_Manchester.jpg" width="220" height="211" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Whitworth_Hall_Manchester.jpg/330px-Whitworth_Hall_Manchester.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Whitworth_Hall_Manchester.jpg/440px-Whitworth_Hall_Manchester.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="615" /></a>/n<div class="thumbcaption">/n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Whitworth_Hall_Manchester.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>/nThe university's <a href="/wiki/Whitworth_Hall" title="Whitworth Hall">Whitworth Hall</a>.</div>/n</div>/n</div>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Finances">Finances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Finances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<p>In the financial year ending 31 July 2011, the University of Manchester had a total income of £808.58&#160;million (2009/10 – £787.9&#160;million) and total expenditure of £754.51&#160;million (2009/10 – £764.55&#160;million).<sup id="cite_ref-finstat_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finstat-1">[1]</a></sup> Key sources of income included £247.28&#160;million from tuition fees and education contracts (2009/10 – £227.75&#160;million), £203.22&#160;million from funding body grants (2009/10 – £209.02&#160;million), £196.24&#160;million from research grants and contracts (2009/10 – £194.6&#160;million) and £14.84&#160;million from endowment and investment income (2009/10 – £11.38&#160;million).<sup id="cite_ref-finstat_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finstat-1">[1]</a></sup> During the 2010/11 financial year the University of Manchester had a capital expenditure of £57.42&#160;million (2009/10 – £37.95&#160;million).<sup id="cite_ref-finstat_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finstat-1">[1]</a></sup></p>/n<p>At year end the University of Manchester had endowments of £158.7&#160;million (2009/10 – £144.37&#160;million) and total net assets of £731.66&#160;million (2009/10 – £677.12&#160;million).<sup id="cite_ref-finstat_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finstat-1">[1]</a></sup></p>/n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academic_profile">Academic profile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Academic profile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>/n<p>The University of Manchester has the largest number of full-time students in the UK, unless the <a href="/wiki/University_of_London" title="University of London">University of London</a>'s colleges are counted as a single university. It teaches more academic subjects than any other British university.</p>/n<p>Well-known figures among the university's current academic staff include computer scientist <a href="/wiki/Steve_Furber" title="Steve Furber">Steve Furber</a>, economist <a href="/wiki/Richard_R._Nelson_(economist)" class="mw-redirect" title="Richard R. Nelson (economist)">Richard Nelson</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> novelist <a href="/wiki/Jeanette_Winterson" title="Jeanette Winterson">Jeanette Winterson</a><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> (who succeeded <a href="/wiki/Colm_T%C3%B3ib%C3%ADn" title="Colm Tóibín">Colm Tóibín</a> in 2012)<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> and biochemist Sir <a href="/wiki/John_Sulston" title="John Sulston">John Sulston</a>, Nobel laureate of 2002.</p>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<p>The University of Manchester is a major centre for research and a member of the <a href="/wiki/Russell_Group" title="Russell Group">Russell Group</a> of leading British research universities.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> In the first national assessment of higher education research since the university's founding, the 2008 <a href="/wiki/Research_Assessment_Exercise" title="Research Assessment Exercise">Research Assessment Exercise</a>, the university was ranked third in terms of research power (after Cambridge and Oxford) and sixth for grade point average quality among multi-faculty institutions<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> (eighth when including specialist institutions)<sup id="cite_ref-timeshighereducation1_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timeshighereducation1-53">[53]</a></sup> Manchester has the fifth largest research income of any British university (after Oxford, Imperial, UCL and Cambridge).<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> (these five universities have been informally referred to as the "golden diamond" of research-intensive UK institutions).<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Manchester has a strong record in terms of securing funding from the three main UK research councils, <a href="/wiki/EPSRC" class="mw-redirect" title="EPSRC">EPSRC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Medical_Research_Council_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="Medical Research Council (UK)">MRC</a> and <a href="/wiki/BBSRC" class="mw-redirect" title="BBSRC">BBSRC</a>, being ranked fifth,<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> seventh<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> and first<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> respectively. In addition, the university is one of the richest in the UK in terms of income and interest from endowments: a recent estimate placed it third, surpassed only by Oxford and Cambridge.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Despite recent severe cuts in higher education Manchester remains at second place behind Oxford nationally in terms of total recurrent grants allocated by the <a href="/wiki/HEFCE" class="mw-redirect" title="HEFCE">HEFCE</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>/n<p>Historically, Manchester has been linked with high scientific achievement: the university and its constituent former institutions combined had <a href="/wiki/University_of_Manchester#Nobel_prize_winners" title="University of Manchester">25 Nobel laureates</a> among their students and staff, the third largest number of any single university in the United Kingdom (after Oxford and Cambridge) and the ninth largest of any university in Europe. Furthermore, according to an academic poll two of the top ten discoveries by university academics and researchers were made at the university (namely the first working computer and the contraceptive pill).<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> The university currently employs four Nobel Prize winners amongst its staff, more than any other in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> The Langworthy Professorship, an endowed chair at the University's School of Physics and Astronomy, has been historically given to a long line of academic luminaries, including Ernest Rutherford (1907–19), Lawrence Bragg (1919–37), Patrick Blackett (1937–53) and more recently Konstantin Novoselov, all of whom have won the Nobel Prize. In 2013 Manchester was given the Regius Professorship in Physics, the only one of its kind in the UK; the current holder is <a href="/wiki/Andre_Geim" title="Andre Geim">Andre Geim</a>.</p>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="University_of_Manchester_Library">University of Manchester Library</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: University of Manchester Library">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<div class="thumb tright">/n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rylands_Library_Deansgate.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Rylands_Library_Deansgate.jpg/220px-Rylands_Library_Deansgate.jpg" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Rylands_Library_Deansgate.jpg/330px-Rylands_Library_Deansgate.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Rylands_Library_Deansgate.jpg/440px-Rylands_Library_Deansgate.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="511" /></a>/n<div class="thumbcaption">/n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rylands_Library_Deansgate.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>/nThe Grade-I listed <a href="/wiki/John_Rylands_Library" title="John Rylands Library">John Rylands Library</a> on Deansgate</div>/n</div>/n</div>/n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/University_of_Manchester_Library" title="University of Manchester Library">University of Manchester Library</a></div>/n<p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Manchester_Library" title="University of Manchester Library">University of Manchester Library</a> is the largest non-<a href="/wiki/Legal_deposit" title="Legal deposit">legal deposit</a> library in the UK and the third-largest academic library after those of <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">Oxford</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">Cambridge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sconul_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sconul-63">[63]</a></sup> It has the largest collection of electronic resources of any library in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-sconul_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sconul-63">[63]</a></sup></p>/n<p>The <a href="/wiki/John_Rylands_Library" title="John Rylands Library">John Rylands Library</a>, founded in memory of <a href="/wiki/John_Rylands" title="John Rylands">John Rylands</a> by his wife <a href="/wiki/Enriqueta_Augustina_Rylands" title="Enriqueta Augustina Rylands">Enriqueta Augustina Rylands</a> as an independent institution, is situated in a <a href="/wiki/Victorian_Gothic" class="mw-redirect" title="Victorian Gothic">Victorian Gothic</a> building on <a href="/wiki/Deansgate" title="Deansgate">Deansgate</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_city_centre" title="Manchester city centre">city centre</a>. It houses an important collection of historic books and other printed materials, manuscripts, including archives and papyri. The papyri are in ancient languages and include the oldest extant <a href="/wiki/New_Testament" title="New Testament">New Testament</a> document, <a href="/wiki/Rylands_Library_Papyrus_P52" title="Rylands Library Papyrus P52">Rylands Library Papyrus P52</a>, commonly known as the <i>St John Fragment</i>. In April 2007 the Deansgate site reopened to readers and the public after major improvements and renovations, including the construction of the pitched roof originally intended and a new wing.</p>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Collections">Collections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Collections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Manchester_Museum">Manchester Museum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Manchester Museum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>/n<div class="thumb tright">/n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_Museum_Entrance.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Manchester_Museum_Entrance.jpg/170px-Manchester_Museum_Entrance.jpg" width="170" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Manchester_Museum_Entrance.jpg/255px-Manchester_Museum_Entrance.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Manchester_Museum_Entrance.jpg/340px-Manchester_Museum_Entrance.jpg 2x" data-file-width="946" data-file-height="945" /></a>/n<div class="thumbcaption">/n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_Museum_Entrance.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>/nThe entrance to the Manchester Museum</div>/n</div>/n</div>/n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Museum" title="Manchester Museum">Manchester Museum</a></div>/n<p>The Manchester Museum holds nearly 4.25 million<sup id="cite_ref-MuseumCollection_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MuseumCollection-64">[64]</a></sup> items sourced from many parts of the world. The collections include butterflies and carvings from India, birds and bark-cloth from the Pacific, live frogs and ancient pottery from America, fossils and native art from Australia, mammals and ancient Egyptian craftsmanship from Africa, plants, coins and minerals from Europe, art from past civilisations of the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean" class="mw-redirect" title="Mediterranean">Mediterranean</a>, and beetles, armour and <a href="/wiki/Archery" title="Archery">archery</a> from Asia. In November 2004, the museum acquired a cast of a fossilised <i><a href="/wiki/Tyrannosaurus" title="Tyrannosaurus">Tyrannosaurus rex</a></i> called "Stan".</p>/n<p>The museum's first collections were assembled in 1821 by the Manchester Society of <a href="/wiki/Natural_History" class="mw-redirect" title="Natural History">Natural History</a>, and subsequently expanded by the addition of the collections of Manchester Geological Society. Due to the society's financial difficulties and on the advice of evolutionary biologist <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Huxley" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomas Huxley">Thomas Huxley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Owens_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Owens College">Owens College</a> accepted responsibility for the collections in 1867. The college commissioned <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Waterhouse" title="Alfred Waterhouse">Alfred Waterhouse</a>, architect of London's <a href="/wiki/Natural_History_Museum,_London" title="Natural History Museum, London">Natural History Museum</a>, to design a museum on a site in Oxford Road to house the collections for the benefit of students and the public. The Manchester Museum was opened to the public in 1888.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>/n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Whitworth_Art_Gallery">Whitworth Art Gallery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Whitworth Art Gallery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>/n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Whitworth_Art_Gallery" title="Whitworth Art Gallery">Whitworth Art Gallery</a></div>/n<div class="thumb tright">/n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Whitworth_Gallery.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Whitworth_Gallery.JPG/220px-Whitworth_Gallery.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Whitworth_Gallery.JPG/330px-Whitworth_Gallery.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Whitworth_Gallery.JPG/440px-Whitworth_Gallery.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>/n<div class="thumbcaption">/n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Whitworth_Gallery.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>/nThe Whitworth Art Gallery</div>/n</div>/n</div>/n<p>The Whitworth Art Gallery houses collections of internationally famous British watercolours, textiles and wallpapers, modern and historic prints, drawings, paintings and sculpture. It contains 31,000 items in its collection. A programme of temporary exhibitions runs throughout the year and the Mezzanine Court displays sculpture. The gallery was founded by Robert Darbishire with a donation from Sir <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Whitworth" title="Joseph Whitworth">Joseph Whitworth</a> in 1889, as <i>The Whitworth Institute and Park</i>. In 1959 the gallery became part of the <a href="/wiki/Victoria_University_of_Manchester" title="Victoria University of Manchester">Victoria University of Manchester</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-history_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-66">[66]</a></sup> In October 1995 the Mezzanine Court in the centre of the building was opened. It was designed to display sculptures and won a <a href="/wiki/Royal_Institute_of_British_Architects" title="Royal Institute of British Architects">RIBA</a> regional award.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rankings_and_reputation">Rankings and reputation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Rankings and reputation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<table class="infobox" style="width:23em; text-align:left; font-size:72%;">/n<caption style="font-size:125%; font-weight:bold;"><a world)</th>/n<td>54=</td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<th scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/CWTS_Leiden_Ranking" title="CWTS Leiden Ranking">CWTS Leiden</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-CWTS_Leiden_Ranking_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CWTS_Leiden_Ranking-73">[73]</a></sup><br />/n(2017, world)</th>/n<td>61</td>/n</tr>/n<tr style="background-color: #e0e0e0;">/n<td colspan="3"></td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<th scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/Rankings_of_universities_in_the_United_Kingdom#The_Complete_University_Guide" title="Rankings of universities in the United Kingdom">Complete</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Complete_League_Table_2018_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Complete_League_Table_2018-74">[74]</a></sup><br />/n(2018,
