Guardian</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-The_Guardian_University_Guide_2018_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Guardian_University_Guide_2018-75">[75]</a></sup><br />/n(2018, national)</th>/n<td>28</td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<th scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/Rankings_of_universities_in_the_United_Kingdom#The_Sunday_Times" title="Rankings of universities in the United Kingdom">Times/Sunday Times</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-The_Times_and_Sunday_Times_University_Guide_2018_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Times_and_Sunday_Times_University_Guide_2018-76">[76]</a></sup><br />/n(2018, national)</th>/n<td>25</td>/n</tr>/n<tr style="background-color: #e0e0e0;">/n<td colspan="3"></td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<th scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/Teaching_Excellence_Framework" title="Teaching Excellence Framework">Teaching Excellence Framework</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-TEF_2017_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TEF_2017-77">[77]</a></sup></th>/n<td><i>Silver</i></td>/n</tr>/n</table>/n<p>In an employability ranking published by Emerging in 2015, where CEOs and chairmen were asked to select the top universities they recruited from, Manchester was placed 24th in the world and 5th nationally.<sup id="cite_ref-Emerging_Rankings_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Emerging_Rankings-78">[78]</a></sup> The Global Employability University Ranking conducted by THE places Manchester at 27th worldwide and 10th in Europe, ahead of academic powerhouses such as Cornell, UPenn and LSE.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> In the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Research_Excellence_Framework" title="Research Excellence Framework">Research Excellence Framework</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-description_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-description-80">[80]</a></sup> Manchester came fifth in terms of research power and seventeenth for grade point average quality when including specialist institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> More students try to gain entry than to any other university in the country, with more than 55,000 applications for undergraduate courses in 2014 resulting in 6.5 applicants for every available place.<sup id="cite_ref-timesonline1_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timesonline1-83">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> According to the 2017 High Fliers Report, Manchester is the second most targeted university by the largest number of leading graduate employers in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>/n<p>According to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sunday_Times_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Sunday Times (UK)">The Sunday Times</a></i>, "Manchester has a formidable reputation spanning most disciplines, but most notably in the life sciences, engineering, humanities, economics, sociology and the social sciences".<sup id="cite_ref-timesonline1_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timesonline1-83">[83]</a></sup> As of 2016, Manchester is ranked as the 8th, 10th and 49th most reputable university in the UK, Europe and the world respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Manchester was also given a prestigious award for Excellence and Innovation in the Arts by the <i>Times Higher Education Awards 2010</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>/n<p>The <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a> 2016-17 placed Manchester 29th in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a> 2016 ranked Manchester 5th in the UK and 35th in the world. Manchester is ranked 56th in the world (and 8th in the UK) in the 2016 <i><a href="/wiki/Round_University_Ranking" title="Round University Ranking">Round University Ranking</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>/n<p>In 2011, the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Business_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Business School">Manchester Business School</a> was ranked 29th worldwide (4th nationally) by the Financial Times in its Global MBA ranking.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> More recently, Alliance Manchester Business is named the 3rd, 10th and 30th Business School in UK, Europe and the World by the Financial Times in its 2017 global MBA ranking.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>/n<p>However, while world rankings (such as QS, ARWU, THE) typically place the university within the top 10 in the UK, in national studies the university ranks less favourably. In <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sunday_Times" title="The Sunday Times">The Sunday Times</a></i> 10-year (1998–2007) average ranking of British universities based on consistent league table performance, Manchester was ranked 17th overall in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> The Times/Sunday Times 'Good University Guide 2015' ranked Manchester 28th out of universities in the UK, 'The Complete University Guide 2016' placed it at 28th, whilst 'The Guardian University Guide 2016' ranked Manchester at 29th in the UK. This apparent paradox is mainly a reflection of the different ranking methodologies employed by each listing: global rankings focus on research and international reputation, whereas national rankings are largely based on entry standards, graduate prospects and student satisfaction with teaching at the university.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Admissions">Admissions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Admissions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<table class="wikitable floatright" style="font-size:85%; text-align:center;">/n<caption>UCAS Admission Statistics</caption>/n<tr>/n<th></th>/n<th>2016</th>/n<th>2015</th>/n<th>2014</th>/n<th>2013</th>/n<th>2012</th>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td><b>Applications</b><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></td>/n<td>63,570</td>/n<td>63,980</td>/n<td>61,285</td>/n<td>55,870</td>/n<td>52,780</td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td><b>Offer Rate (%)</b><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></td>/n<td>72.4</td>/n<td>73.4</td>/n<td>72.6</td>/n<td>72.6</td>/n<td>68.9</td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td><b>Enrols</b><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></td>/n<td>8,705</td>/n<td>9,330</td>/n<td>9,040</td>/n<td>8,605</td>/n<td>7,860</td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td><a href="/wiki/Yield_(college_admissions)" title="Yield (college admissions)"><b>Yield (%)</b></a></td>/n<td>18.9</td>/n<td>19.9</td>/n<td>20.3</td>/n<td>21.2</td>/n<td>21.6</td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td><b>Applicant/Enrolled Ratio</b></td>/n<td>7.30</td>/n<td>6.86</td>/n<td>6.78</td>/n<td>6.49</td>/n<td>6.72</td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td><b><a href="/wiki/UCAS_Tariff" title="UCAS Tariff">Average Entry Tariff</a></b><sup id="cite_ref-Complete_League_Table_2018_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Complete_League_Table_2018-74">[74]</a></sup></td>/n<td>n/a</td>/n<td>431</td>/n<td>435</td>/n<td>433</td>/n<td>441</td>/n</tr>/n</table>/n<p>Manchester had the 17th highest average entry qualification for undergraduates of any UK university in 2015, with new students averaging 431 UCAS points,<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> equivalent to just above ABBab in <a href="/wiki/GCE_Advanced_Level_(United_Kingdom)" title="GCE Advanced Level (United Kingdom)">A-level</a> grades. According to the 2017 <i>Times</i> and <i>Sunday Times</i> Good University Guide, approximately 18% of Manchester's undergraduates come from independent schools.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>/n<p>The university gives offers of admission to 73.4% of its applicants, the 10th lowest amongst the <a href="/wiki/Russell_Group" title="Russell Group">Russell Group</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manchester_University_Press">Manchester University Press</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Manchester University Press">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Manchester_University_Press" title="Manchester University Press">Manchester University Press</a></div>/n<p><a href="/wiki/Manchester_University_Press" title="Manchester University Press">Manchester University Press</a> is the university's academic publishing house. It publishes academic <a href="/wiki/Monograph" title="Monograph">monographs</a>, textbooks and journals, most of which are works from authors based elsewhere in the international academic community, and is the third-largest university press in England after <a href="/wiki/Oxford_University_Press" title="Oxford University Press">Oxford University Press</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_University_Press" title="Cambridge University Press">Cambridge University Press</a>.</p>/n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>/n<h3><span id="Students'_Union"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Students.27_Union">Students' Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Students' Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<div class="thumb tright">/n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_University_Students_Union_Building_(geograph_1963615).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Manchester_University_Students_Union_Building_%28geograph_1963615%29.jpg/250px-Manchester_University_Students_Union_Building_%28geograph_1963615%29.jpg" width="250" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Manchester_University_Students_Union_Building_%28geograph_1963615%29.jpg/375px-Manchester_University_Students_Union_Building_%28geograph_1963615%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Manchester_University_Students_Union_Building_%28geograph_1963615%29.jpg/500px-Manchester_University_Students_Union_Building_%28geograph_1963615%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1028" data-file-height="600" /></a>/n<div class="thumbcaption">/n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_University_Students_Union_Building_(geograph_1963615).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>/nThe Students' Union building on Oxford Road</div>/n</div>/n</div>/n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/University_of_Manchester_Students%27_Union" title="University of Manchester Students' Union">University of Manchester Students' Union</a></div>/n<p>The University of Manchester Students' Union is the representative body of students at the university and the UK's largest students' union. It was formed out of the merger between UMIST Students' Association and University of Manchester Union when the parent organisations UMIST and the Victoria University of Manchester merged on 1 October 2004.</p>/n<p>Unlike many other students' unions in the UK, it does not have a president, but is run by an 8-member executive team who share joint responsibility.</p>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<div class="thumb tright">/n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_University_Boat_Club.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Manchester_University_Boat_Club.jpg/250px-Manchester_University_Boat_Club.jpg" width="250" height="93" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Manchester_University_Boat_Club.jpg/375px-Manchester_University_Boat_Club.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Manchester_University_Boat_Club.jpg/500px-Manchester_University_Boat_Club.jpg 2x" data-file-width="850" data-file-height="317" /></a>/n<div class="thumbcaption">/n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_University_Boat_Club.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>/nThe University's Boat Club is one of many Athletic Union Clubs that Manchester offers.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></div>/n</div>/n</div>/n<p>The University of Manchester operates sports clubs via the <a href="/wiki/Athletics_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Athletics Union">Athletics Union</a> while student societies are operated by the Students' Union.</p>/n<p>The university has more than 80 health and fitness classes while over 3,000 students are members of the 44 various Athletic Union clubs. The sports societies vary widely in their level and scope. Many more popular sports operate several university teams and departmental teams which compete in leagues against other teams within the university. Teams include: <a href="/wiki/Lacrosse" title="Lacrosse">lacrosse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Korfball" title="Korfball">korfball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dodgeball" title="Dodgeball">dodgeball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hockey" title="Hockey">hockey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>, basketball, <a href="/wiki/Netball" title="Netball">netball</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Aquatics_Centre" title="Manchester Aquatics Centre">Manchester Aquatics Centre</a>, the swimming pool used for the <a href="/wiki/2002_Commonwealth_Games" title="2002 Commonwealth Games">Manchester Commonwealth Games</a> is on the campus.</p>/n<p>The university competes annually in 28 different sports against <a href="/wiki/University_of_Leeds" title="University of Leeds">Leeds</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Liverpool" title="University of Liverpool">Liverpool</a> universities in the <a href="/wiki/Christie_Cup" title="Christie Cup">Christie Cup</a>, which Manchester has won for seven consecutive years.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> The university has achieved success in the <a href="/wiki/British_Universities_%26_Colleges_Sport" class="mw-redirect" title="British Universities &amp; Colleges Sport">BUCS</a> (British University &amp; College Sports) competitions, with its men's <a href="/wiki/Water_polo" title="Water polo">water polo</a> 1st team winning the national championships (2009, 2010, 2011) under the tutelage of coach Andy Howard.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> It was positioned in eighth place in the overall BUCS rankings for 2009/10<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Christie_Cup" title="Christie Cup">Christie Cup</a> is an inter-university competition between Liverpool, Leeds and Manchester in numerous sports since 1886. After the <a href="/wiki/Oxford_and_Cambridge_rivalry" class="mw-redirect" title="Oxford and Cambridge rivalry">Oxford and Cambridge rivalry</a>, the Christie's Championships is the oldest Inter–University competition on the sporting calendar: the cup was a benefaction of <a href="/wiki/Richard_Copley_Christie" title="Richard Copley Christie">Richard Copley Christie</a>.</p>/n<p>Every year elite sportsmen and sportswomen are selected for membership of the <i>XXI Club</i>, a society formed in 1932 to promote sporting excellence at the university. Most members have gained a <a href="/wiki/Blue_(university_sport)" title="Blue (university sport)">Full Maroon</a> for representing the university and many have excelled at a British Universities or National level.</p>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="University_Challenge_quiz_programme"><i>University Challenge</i> quiz programme</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: University Challenge quiz programme">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<p>In the eight years up to 2013 Manchester have won the <a href="/wiki/BBC_Two" title="BBC Two">BBC2</a> quiz programme <i><a href="/wiki/University_Challenge" title="University Challenge">University Challenge</a></i> four times, drawing equal with <a href="/wiki/Magdalen_College,_Oxford" title="Magdalen College, Oxford">Magdalen College, Oxford</a>, for the highest number of series wins.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> Since merging as the University of Manchester, the university has consistently reached the latter stages of the competition, progressing to at least the semi-finals every year since 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-challenge_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-challenge-105">[105]</a></sup></p>/n<p>In <a href="/wiki/University_Challenge_2006" class="mw-redirect" title="University Challenge 2006">2006</a>, Manchester beat <a href="/wiki/Trinity_Hall,_Cambridge" title="Trinity Hall, Cambridge">Trinity Hall, Cambridge</a>, to record the university's first win in the competition. The <a href="/wiki/University_Challenge_2007" class="mw-redirect" title="University Challenge 2007">next year</a>, the university finished in second place after losing to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Warwick" title="University of Warwick">University of Warwick</a> in the final. In <a href="/wiki/University_Challenge_2009" class="mw-redirect" title="University Challenge 2009">2009</a>, the team battled hard in the final against <a href="/wiki/Corpus_Christi_College,_Oxford" title="Corpus Christi College, Oxford">Corpus Christi College, Oxford</a>. At the gong, the score was 275 to 190 in favour of Corpus Christi College after a winning performance from <a href="/wiki/Gail_Trimble" title="Gail Trimble">Gail Trimble</a>. However, the title was eventually given to the University of Manchester after it was discovered that Corpus Christi team member Sam Kay had graduated eight months before the final was broadcast, so the team was disqualified.</p>/n<p>Manchester reached the semi-finals in the <a href="/wiki/University_Challenge_2010" class="mw-redirect" title="University Challenge 2010">2010</a> competition before being beaten by <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_College,_Cambridge" title="Emmanuel College, Cambridge">Emmanuel College, Cambridge</a>. The university did not enter the <a href="/wiki/University_Challenge_2010%E2%80%9311" title="University Challenge 2010–11">2011 series</a> for an unknown reason. However, Manchester did enter a year later and won <a href="/wiki/University_Challenge_2012" class="mw-redirect" title="University Challenge 2012">University Challenge 2012</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-challenge_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-challenge-105">[105]</a></sup> Manchester has since defended its title to win <a href="/wiki/University_Challenge_2013" class="mw-redirect" title="University Challenge 2013">University Challenge 2013</a>, beating <a href="/wiki/University_College_London" title="University College London">University College London</a>, 190 to 140.</p>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overseas_students">Overseas students</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Overseas students">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<p>The University of Manchester attracts thousands of international students coming from 156 countries around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_housing">Student housing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Student housing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<div class="thumb tright">/n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ManUni_Accommodation_year1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2f/ManUni_Accommodation_year1.jpg/220px-ManUni_Accommodation_year1.jpg" width="220" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2f/ManUni_Accommodation_year1.jpg/330px-ManUni_Accommodation_year1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2f/ManUni_Accommodation_year1.jpg/440px-ManUni_Accommodation_year1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="754" data-file-height="437" /></a>/n<div class="thumbcaption">/n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ManUni_Accommodation_year1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>/nAshburne Hall, a catered accommodation offered mainly to undergraduate students, though some places are reserved for postgraduate students</div>/n</div>/n</div>/n<p>Before they merged, the two former universities had for some time been sharing their residential facilities.</p>/n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="City_Campus">City Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: City Campus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>/n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Whitworth_Park_Halls_of_Residence">Whitworth Park Halls of Residence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Whitworth Park Halls of Residence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>/n<p>Whitworth Park Halls of Residence is owned by the University of Manchester and houses 1,085 students.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> It is notable for its triangular shaped accommodation blocks which gave rise to the nickname of "Toblerones", after the <a href="/wiki/Toblerone" title="Toblerone">chocolate bar</a>. Their designer took inspiration from a hill created from excavated soil which had been left in 1962 from an archaeological dig led by John Gater. A consequence of the triangular design was a reduced cost for the construction company. A deal struck between the university and Manchester City Council meant the council would pay for the roofs of all student residential buildings in the area, Allan Pluen's team is believed to have saved thousands on the final cost of the halls. They were built in the mid-1970s.</p>/n<div class="thumb tright">/n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Whitworth_Park_Halls.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Whitworth_Park_Halls.jpg/220px-Whitworth_Park_Halls.jpg" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Whitworth_Park_Halls.jpg/330px-Whitworth_Park_Halls.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Whitworth_Park_Halls.jpg/440px-Whitworth_Park_Halls.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1446" /></a>/n<div class="thumbcaption">/n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Whitworth_Park_Halls.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>/nDilworth House, one of the Whitworth Park halls of residence</div>/n</div>/n</div>/n<p>The site of the halls was previously occupied by many small streets whose names have been preserved in the names of the halls. Grove House is an older building that has been used by the university for many different purposes over the last sixty years. Its first occupants in 1951 were the Appointments Board and the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_University_Press" title="Manchester University Press">Manchester University Press</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> The shops in Thorncliffe Place were part of the same plan and include banks and a convenience store. Notable people associated with the halls include <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Engels" title="Friedrich Engels">Friedrich Engels</a>, whose residence is commemorated by a blue plaque on Aberdeen House; the physicist <a href="/wiki/Brian_Cox_(physicist)" title="Brian Cox (physicist)">Brian Cox</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Irene_Khan" title="Irene Khan">Irene Khan</a>, Secretary General of Amnesty International.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>/n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Sackville_Street">Sackville Street</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Sackville Street">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>/n<p>The former UMIST Campus has five halls of residence near to <a href="/wiki/Sackville_Street_(Manchester)" title="Sackville Street (Manchester)">Sackville Street</a> building (Weston, Lambert, Fairfield, Chandos, and Wright Robinson), and several other halls within a 5–15-minute walk, such as the Grosvenor group of halls.</p>/n<dl>/n<dt>Other accommodation</dt>/n</dl>/n<p>Moberly Tower has been demolished. Other residences include Vaughn House, once the home of the clergy serving the Church of the Holy Name, and George Kenyon Hall at University Place; Crawford House and Devonshire House adjacent to the Manchester Business School and Victoria Hall on Upper Brook Street.</p>/n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Victoria_Park_Campus">Victoria Park Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Victoria Park Campus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>/n<p><a href="/wiki/Victoria_Park,_Manchester" title="Victoria Park, Manchester">Victoria Park</a> Campus comprises several halls of residence. Among these are <a href="/wiki/St._Anselm_Hall" title="St. Anselm Hall">St. Anselm Hall</a> with Canterbury Court and Pankhurst Court, <a href="/wiki/Dalton-Ellis_Hall" title="Dalton-Ellis Hall">Dalton-Ellis Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hulme_Hall,_Manchester" title="Hulme Hall, Manchester">Hulme Hall</a> (including Burkhardt House), <a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Gabriel%27s_Hall&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="St Gabriel's Hall (page does not exist)">St Gabriel's Hall</a> and Opal Gardens Hall. St. Anselm Hall is the only all-male hall in the United Kingdom.</p>/n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fallowfield_Campus">Fallowfield Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Fallowfield Campus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>/n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Fallowfield_Campus" title="Fallowfield Campus">Fallowfield Campus</a>, 2 miles (3.2&#160;km) south of the Oxford Road Campus is the largest of the university's residential campuses. The <a href="/wiki/Owens_Park" title="Owens Park">Owens Park</a> group of halls with a landmark tower is at its centre, while <a href="/w/index.php?title=Oak_House&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Oak House (page does not exist)">Oak House</a> is another hall of residence. Woolton Hall is next to Oak House. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Allen_Hall_(University_of_Manchester)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Allen Hall (University of Manchester) (page does not exist)">Allen Hall</a> is a traditional hall near <a href="/wiki/Ashburne_Hall" title="Ashburne Hall">Ashburne Hall</a> (Sheavyn House being annexed to Ashburne). Richmond Park is a recent addition to the campus.</p>/n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>/n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Manchester_people" title="List of University of Manchester people">List of University of Manchester people</a></div>/n<p>Many notable people have worked or studied at one or both of the two former institutions that now form the University of Manchester, including 25 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_prize" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobel prize">Nobel prize</a> laureates. Some of the best-known are: <a href="/wiki/John_Dalton" title="John Dalton">John Dalton</a> (founder of modern atomic theory), <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Rutherford" title="Ernest Rutherford">Ernest Rutherford</a> who proved the nuclear nature of the atom whilst working at Manchester, <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_Wittgenstein" title="Ludwig Wittgenstein">Ludwig Wittgenstein</a> (considered one of the most significant philosophers of the 20th century, who studied for a doctorate in engineering), <a href="/wiki/George_E._Davis" title="George E. Davis">George E. Davis</a> (founder of the discipline of <a href="/wiki/Chemical_Engineering" class="mw-redirect" title="Chemical Engineering">Chemical Engineering</a>), <a href="/wiki/Marie_Stopes" title="Marie Stopes">Marie Stopes</a> (pioneer of birth control and campaigner for women's rights), <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Lovell" title="Bernard Lovell">Bernard Lovell</a> (a pioneer of <a href="/wiki/Radio_astronomy" title="Radio astronomy">radio astronomy</a>), <a href="/wiki/Alan_Turing" title="Alan Turing">Alan Turing</a> (one of the founders of <a href="/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">computer science</a> and <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>), <a href="/wiki/Tom_Kilburn" title="Tom Kilburn">Tom Kilburn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frederic_Calland_Williams" title="Frederic Calland Williams">Frederic Calland Williams</a> (who developed <a href="/wiki/Small-Scale_Experimental_Machine" class="mw-redirect" title="Small-Scale Experimental Machine">Small-Scale Experimental Machine</a> (SSEM) or "Baby", the world's first stored-program computer at <a href="/wiki/Victoria_University_of_Manchester" title="Victoria University of Manchester">Victoria University of Manchester</a> in 1948), <a href="/wiki/Irene_Khan" title="Irene Khan">Irene Khan</a> (former Secretary General of <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a>), physicist and television presenter <a href="/wiki/Brian_Cox_(physicist)" title="Brian Cox (physicist)">Brian Cox</a>, the author <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Burgess" title="Anthony Burgess">Anthony Burgess</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Bolt" title="Robert Bolt">Robert Bolt</a> (two times <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> winner and three times <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Globe">Golden Globe</a> winner for writing the screenplay for <i><a href="/wiki/Lawrence_of_Arabia_(film)" title="Lawrence of Arabia (film)">Lawrence of Arabia</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Doctor_Zhivago_(film)" title="Doctor Zhivago (film)">Doctor Zhivago</a></i>).</p>/n<p>A number of politicians are associated with the university, including the current presidents of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Somaliland" title="Somaliland">Somaliland</a> region of <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a> and prime ministers of <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_territories" title="Palestinian territories">Palestine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, as well as several ministers in the United Kingdom, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, Canada, Singapore and Sri Lanka. The vice president of Tanzania (November 2015 – present), <a href="/wiki/Samia_Hassan_Suluhu" class="mw-redirect" title="Samia Hassan Suluhu">Samia Hassan Suluhu</a>, also attended the University of Manchester. <a href="/wiki/Chaim_Weizmann" title="Chaim Weizmann">Chaim Weizmann</a>, a senior lecturer at the university, was also the first President of <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>. The Vice General Secretary of State of Sri Lanka, (October 2017 – present</p>/n<p>The university educated some of the leading figures of <a href="/wiki/Alternative_Comedy" class="mw-redirect" title="Alternative Comedy">Alternative Comedy</a>: <a href="/wiki/Ben_Elton" title="Ben Elton">Ben Elton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ade_Edmonson" class="mw-redirect" title="Ade Edmonson">Ade Edmonson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rik_Mayall" title="Rik Mayall">Rik Mayall</a>. Additionally, a number of well-known actors have studied at the university, including <a href="/wiki/Benedict_Cumberbatch" title="Benedict Cumberbatch">Benedict Cumberbatch</a>, who most notably portrays <a href="/wiki/Sherlock_Holmes" title="Sherlock Holmes">Sherlock Holmes</a> in the TV series <i><a href="/wiki/Sherlock_(TV_series)" title="Sherlock (TV series)">Sherlock</a></i>, as well as playing the role of Manchester's own <a href="/wiki/Alan_Turing" title="Alan Turing">Alan Turing</a> in the 2014 Oscar-winning biopic <i><a href="/wiki/The_Imitation_Game" title="The Imitation Game">The Imitation Game</a></i>.</p>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nobel_prize_winners">Nobel prize winners</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Nobel prize winners">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<p>The University of Manchester, inclusive of its predecessor institutions, numbers 25 Nobel Prize recipients amongst its current and former staff and students, with some of the most important discoveries of the modern age having been made in Manchester. Manchester University has the third largest number of Nobel laureates in the UK, only Cambridge and Oxford universities having a greater number.</p>/n<p><b>Chemistry</b></p>/n<ul>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Ernest_Rutherford" title="Ernest Rutherford">Ernest Rutherford</a> (awarded Nobel prize in 1908), for his investigations into the disintegration of the elements and the chemistry of radioactive substances.</li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Arthur_Harden" title="Arthur Harden">Arthur Harden</a> (awarded Nobel prize in 1929), for investigations on the fermentation of sugar and fermentative enzymes.</li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Walter_Haworth" class="mw-redirect" title="Walter Haworth">Walter Haworth</a> (awarded Nobel prize in 1937), for his investigations on carbohydrates and vitamin C.</li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/George_de_Hevesy" title="George de Hevesy">George de Hevesy</a> (awarded Nobel prize in 1943), for his work on the use of isotopes as tracers in the study of chemical processes.</li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_Robinson_(organic_chemist)" title="Robert Robinson (organic chemist)">Robert Robinson</a> (awarded Nobel prize in 1947), for his investigations on plant products of biological importance, especially the alkaloids.</li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Alexander_R._Todd,_Baron_Todd" class="mw-redirect" title="Alexander R. Todd, Baron Todd">Alexander Todd</a> (awarded Nobel prize in 1957), for his work on nucleotides and nucleotide co-enzymes.</li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Melvin_Calvin" title="Melvin Calvin">Melvin Calvin</a> (awarded Nobel prize in 1961), for his research on the carbon dioxide assimilation in plants.</li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/John_Charles_Polanyi" class="mw-redirect" title="John Charles Polanyi">John Charles Polanyi</a> (awarded Nobel prize in 1986), for his contributions concerning the dynamics of chemical elementary processes.</li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Michael_Smith_(chemist)" title="Michael Smith (chemist)">Michael Smith</a> (awarded Nobel prize in 1993), for his fundamental contributions to the establishment of <a href="/wiki/Oligonucleotide" title="Oligonucleotide">oligonucleotide</a>-based, site-directed mutagenesis and its development for protein studies.</li>/n</ul>/n<p><b>Physics</b></p>/n<ul>/n<li><a href="/wiki/J._J._Thomson" title="J. J. Thomson">Joseph John (J. J.) Thomson</a> (awarded Nobel prize in 1906), in recognition of his theoretical and experimental investigations on the conduction of electricity by gases.</li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/William_Lawrence_Bragg" title="William Lawrence Bragg">William Lawrence Bragg</a> (awarded Nobel prize in 1915), for his services in the analysis of crystal structure by means of X-rays.</li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Niels_Bohr" title="Niels Bohr">Niels Bohr</a> (awarded Nobel prize in 1922), for his fundamental contributions to understanding atomic structure and quantum mechanics.</li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Charles_Thomson_Rees_Wilson" title="Charles Thomson Rees Wilson">Charles Thomson Rees (C. T. R.) Wilson</a> (awarded Nobel prize in 1927), for his method of making the paths of electrically charged particles visible by condensation of vapour.</li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/James_Chadwick" title="James Chadwick">James Chadwick</a> (awarded Nobel prize in 1935), for the discovery of the <a href="/wiki/Neutron" title="Neutron">neutron</a>.</li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Patrick_Maynard_Stuart_Blackett" class="mw-redirect" title="Patrick Maynard Stuart Blackett">Patrick M. Blackett</a> (awarded Nobel prize in 1948), for developing cloud chamber and confirming/discovering positron.</li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Sir_John_Douglas_Cockcroft" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir John Douglas Cockcroft">Sir John Douglas Cockcroft</a> (awarded Nobel prize in 1951), for his pioneer work on the splitting of atomic nuclei by artificially accelerated atomic particles and also for his contribution to modern nuclear power.</li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Hans_Bethe" title="Hans Bethe">Hans Bethe</a> (awarded Nobel prize in 1967), for his contributions to the theory of nuclear reactions, especially his discoveries concerning the energy production in stars.</li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Nevill_Francis_Mott" title="Nevill Francis Mott">Nevill Francis Mott</a> (awarded Nobel prize in 1977), for his fundamental theoretical investigations of the electronic structure of magnetic and disordered systems.</li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Andre_Geim" title="Andre Geim">Andre Geim</a> and <a href="/wiki/Konstantin_Novoselov" title="Konstantin Novoselov">Konstantin Novoselov</a> (awarded Nobel prize in 2010), for groundbreaking experiments regarding the two-dimensional material <a href="/wiki/Graphene" title="Graphene">graphene</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></li>/n</ul>/n<p><b>Physiology and Medicine</b></p>/n<ul>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Archibald_Vivian_Hill" class="mw-redirect" title="Archibald Vivian Hill">Archibald Vivian Hill</a> (awarded Nobel prize in 1922), for his discovery relating to the production of heat in muscle. One of the founders of the diverse disciplines of biophysics and operations research.</li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/John_Sulston" title="John Sulston">Sir John Sulston</a> (awarded Nobel prize in 2002), for his discoveries concerning 'genetic regulation of organ development and programmed cell death'. In 2007, Sulston was announced as Chair of the newly founded <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Science,_Ethics_and_Innovation" title="Institute for Science, Ethics and Innovation">Institute for Science, Ethics and Innovation</a> (iSEI) at the University of Manchester.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></li>/n</ul>/n<p><b>Economics</b></p>/n<ul>/n<li><a href="/wiki/John_Hicks" title="John Hicks">John Hicks</a> (awarded Nobel prize in 1972), for his pioneering contributions to general economic equilibrium theory and welfare theory.</li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Sir_Arthur_Lewis" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Arthur Lewis">Sir Arthur Lewis</a> (awarded Nobel prize in 1979), for his pioneering research into economic development research with particular consideration of the problems of developing countries.</li>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Joseph_E._Stiglitz" class="mw-redirect" title="Joseph E. Stiglitz">Joseph E. Stiglitz</a> (awarded Nobel prize in 2001), for his analyses of markets with asymmetric information. Currently heads the <a href="/wiki/Brooks_World_Poverty_Institute" title="Brooks World Poverty Institute">Brooks World Poverty Institute</a> (BWPI) at the University of Manchester.</li>/n</ul>/n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>/n<ul>/n<li><a href="/wiki/Third-oldest_university_in_England_debate" title="Third-oldest university in England debate">Third-oldest university in England debate</a></li>/n</ul>/n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Manchester&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>/n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">/n<ol class="references">/n<li id="cite_note-finstat-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-finstat_1-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-finstat_1-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-finstat_1-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-finstat_1-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-finstat_1-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-finstat_1-5"><sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-finstat_1-6"><sup><i><b>g</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://documents.manchester.ac.uk/display.aspx?DocID=30586">"Financial statements for the year ended 31 July 2016"</a>.
